Notes on Chu Minyi's Speech at the Global Student Association

At 7:00 PM last night, Central Committee member Chu Minyi, at the invitation of the Global Chinese Student Association, came to the association to give a speech entitled [Methods and Purposes of Physical Education]. In addition to members of the association, students from more than a dozen well-known universities in this city were present, and the hall was already full before 7:00 PM. After Chairman Zhu Shaoping gave a speech, Mr. Chu was invited to speak. The following is a brief record of his speech: [The purpose of physical education is to maintain our health permanently. As Western philosophers have said, "A sound mind dwells in a sound body." Only when our physique is sound can we be motivated to act with vigor. Examining the techniques of various sports, such as ball games, track and field, martial arts, gymnastics, as well as horse racing, boat racing, and swimming, cannot be said to be non-physical education methods. However, their methods are not perfect, and may even be too intense, leading to harm to the body, which runs counter to the original purpose of physical education. Therefore, the physical education methods that I advocate are pure, peaceful, leisurely, and simple. Their function is to make the muscles and bones of the whole body move and the meridians relaxed. They do not value the fierce and dangerous movements of leaping and kicking. Only in this way can the goal of improving health be achieved. In terms of methods, Taijiquan is the best. Taijiquan has three major advantages: time efficiency, money efficiency, and energy efficiency, which other sports cannot match. I will explain them separately as follows: (1) Other sports take a lot of time, and most of them are biased towards one part, inevitably leading to neglect of the others. If Taijiquan, it can be completed in five minutes. Twenty minutes a day is more than enough, and it can make the muscles and bones of the whole body move and the meridians relaxed. There is no time efficiency better than this. (2) The modern social economic organization is poor, and the gap between the rich and the poor is huge. In terms of physical education, the poor who intend to practice self-cultivation in mild exercise are often discouraged because they cannot afford to buy equipment. As for the movement of ball fields, ships, and carriages, it is only enjoyed by a few people, and the poor have no part in it. Taijiquan does not require expensive tools, only two kinds of balls and sticks. It can be done independently or jointly with the public. It does not require a wide field and can be done indoors. It does not require a special teacher and can be obtained privately. There is no money efficiency better than Taijiquan. (3) All sports require effort, especially intense sports. Too much effort will inevitably lead to fatigue, which indirectly reduces the power of social service and directly harms the individual's physiology. Our strength is so precious, how can we waste it on exercise, not knowing the way of economy, and contrary to the purpose of exercise? Taijiquan does not waste useful strength, is neutral, peaceful, leisurely, and unhurried, and is the most active exercise among soft exercises. It can prevent paralysis in old age and become a useless person. This is the most appropriate conditioning method and a preventive method for diseases. Excessive exercise and excessive work for laborers have the same destination. People always think that the more labor, the more the production efficiency will increase, but they do not know that the opposite is true. Taijiquan not only saves strength but also stores strength. Energy efficiency is rare. The function of Taijiquan is so great, but people may be afraid of difficulty and dislike a section, which takes a month to complete, and the full achievement is not easy, so they retreat and discourage. Regarding this point, I have already found a quick method and a remedial method, and created simple equipment for people to exercise on their own. There is no need for regular learners to follow the steps and abide by the rules. Spend a few minutes a day to pass the time on this. If you practice for a long time, you will naturally become healthier. Finally, the two kinds of ball sticks used in Taiji New and the manufacturing and application methods of the equipment are very detailed. (Detailed speeches will be published in the publications of the association.) After the speech, the audience stood up and thanked Mr. Chu and dispersed.

Huang Jiaohui Discusses the Opium Disaster in the Malay Peninsula

The opium disaster in the East Indies has been reported in previous newspapers by Huang Jiaohui, the director-general of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, who was sent to Nanyang for investigation and reported to the association's staff. Huang's investigation into the opium disaster in the British Malay Peninsula was particularly detailed, and he obtained a wealth of materials. Yesterday, he briefly described the following to the association. There are more than two million overseas Chinese in the Malay Peninsula and the Straits Settlements. There are no accurate statistics on smokers, but according to reliable estimates, at least 20% of the population smokes opium. In comparison to China, the situation is even more serious. There are virtually no Malay natives who smoke opium. Almost all of the victims are overseas Chinese. According to a survey of the population, only 13% of overseas Chinese smoke opium. A survey of smokers in opium dens found that 80% of them became addicted to opium after arriving in British territory. A survey of smokers in various hospitals found that 71% of them became addicted after arriving in British territory. It can be seen that the monopoly system has a great relationship with the spread of opium addiction among overseas Chinese. According to survey statistics, in 1928, the Straits Settlements Government Monopoly Bureau purchased 2,027 boxes of Indian opium and 950 boxes of Persian opium, for a total of 2,977 boxes. The public sales bureau produced and sold 3,199,998 taels of opium. In addition, 13,551 taels of privately obtained opium were found and transferred to public sales. The government set up public sales stores and opium dens in bustling markets, paying particular attention to factories, workplaces, rubber plantations, and tin mines. Government opium revenue accounted for 40% of the total revenue. In 1928, the total revenue of the Straits Settlements was 12,222,263 yuan, the Federated Malay States 11,782,128 yuan, Kedah 2,052,564 yuan, Kelantan 4,355,848 yuan, Terengganu 291,570 yuan, Perlis 206,508 yuan, Johor 4,224,465 yuan, Brunei 79,447 yuan, British North Borneo 93,498 yuan, Sarawak 951,118 yuan, and Hong Kong 2,582,101 yuan, totaling 35,021,510 yuan, equivalent to approximately 50 million Chinese yuan. In 1929, the Straits Settlements' opium revenue was 9.6 million yuan, and the budgeted revenue for 1930 increased to 12.75 million yuan. Other places are not included. It can be seen that the local government has no sincerity in prohibiting opium. In terms of tax revenue, the government currently has accumulated tax revenue exceeding the administrative expenses by 72 million yuan, a currency surplus of 21 million yuan, and accumulated opium tax revenue of 44 million yuan, for a total of 138 million yuan. The interest from this huge sum is enough to offset the opium tax and more, but the authorities are still trying to expand opium sales and add opium dens, which is alarming. Previously, an overseas Chinese in British territory had established anti-drug organizations in many places, advocating opium cessation and sparing no effort. However, after repeated unexpected obstacles, it was discontinued. This time, Mr. Huang went to various places in British territory to discuss the organization of anti-drug organizations with important overseas Chinese figures and public groups, which was well received. Various groups and local dignitaries in Singapore have jointly organized an anti-drug association and are actively proceeding. It is expected that other places will soon follow. It is heard that Mr. Huang's detailed report is currently being compiled.

Local News Two

Xie Baosheng's Son, Comprador of Xinming Shipping Company, Kidnapped

▲Sudden Attack During the One-Month-Old Celebration Banquet

▲Guests Closely Monitored, Serious Situation

▲Kidnapping and Robbery at Sea, Unheard Of

▲Bandits' Cunning Plan for an Easy Escape

Yesterday afternoon at 7:30 PM, a kidnapping case of a seven-year-old boy occurred at No. 871, Qunshou Lane, Baker Road. The kidnapped boy was Songtao, the son of Mr. Xie Baosheng, the comprador of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming ship. The kidnappers also robbed gold and silver jewelry, clothing, and other items. The details are recorded separately below.

▲Banquet Full of Guests and Friends Xie Baosheng is well-known at sea and has many friends. His old residence was originally at No. 739, Wufu Lane, Avenue Edward VII. His concubine, Ms. Li, is the daughter of yarn merchant Mr. Li Mingzhai. Ms. Li lives at No. 817, Qunshou Lane, Baker Road. Ms. Li also lives in her mother's home and has two sons. The elder is Songtao, who was kidnapped, is seven years old, and the younger one was recently born and has just turned one month old. A large one-month-old celebration banquet was held at home in the evening, with the banquet full of guests and friends, totaling about twenty people. While everyone was cheering and drinking, six uninvited guests suddenly broke in. The guests initially thought they were more guests coming to congratulate them, and paid no attention.

▲All Guests Closely Monitored Who knew that four of the newcomers were dressed neatly, but the host did not entertain them, and the guests did not immediately take their seats. The guests were wondering what was going on. At this moment, the neatly dressed newcomers suddenly pulled out pistols and monitored Li Mingzhai's actions. Only then did the guests realize the seriousness of the situation and had to remain silent, temporarily losing their freedom. Two more uninvited guests, taking advantage of this serious situation, also drew their guns and hurried upstairs.

▲Two Suitcases of Clothes and Jewelry Taken Upstairs At that time, there was no one upstairs. The two uninvited guests grabbed two suitcases and carried them downstairs. Judging by the intent of the uninvited guests, they initially intended to kidnap someone but did not intend to rob anything. However, because there were so many guests and many children, they could not find a hostage in a hurry, which led to unexpected complications. They first grabbed the suitcases. The suitcases contained valuable leather clothing and jewelry. After the two uninvited guests carried the suitcases downstairs, they went directly to the courtyard, threw the two suitcases on the ground, opened them with force, and arbitrarily searched for clothing and jewelry. Everyone was still under surveillance and could do nothing about it. The hostage, Songtao, was also identified by the thieves among the people.

▲Living Hostage Captured On the Spot While the two uninvited guests were taking clothes and jewelry, the four uninvited guests monitoring the room also acted together, grabbing Songtao and taking him out. Everyone in the room could not help. Ms. Li wanted to cry but had no tears, and was extremely frightened. The maternal grandfather, Mingzhai, with his old eyes and poor vision, trembled almost without color. The two uninvited guests in the courtyard, after the hostage was taken away for ten minutes, also packed up their loot, concealed their pistols, and added Mingzhai's fox fur coat to themselves. However, the size did not fit, so they reluctantly put it on, preparing to leave.

▲Trying to Chase the Bandits' Scheme At that time, Ms. Li's younger brother, seeing that the uninvited guests had concealed their pistols, suddenly became bold. He followed them out, and the guests followed behind him. Seeing that the pursuers were close, the bandits, fearing arrest, had an idea. They immediately stopped, took off the fox fur coat, and threw it on the road, preparing to counterattack. Ms. Li's younger brother, fearing that they would take out their pistols again and be killed, had to retreat. However, the bandits dared to chase back. At that time, a patrolling Indian constable with a pistol happened to be passing by. He mistakenly thought that Li's younger brother was a thief. When Li's younger brother saw the Indian constable, he shouted wildly, "Kidnapping!" However, the Indian constable still could not distinguish the truth from falsehood. In the blink of an eye, the bandits took the opportunity to escape without a trace. ▲Reporting to the Police Station and Requesting Investigation Afterwards, Ms. Li's younger brother reported to the Xinzha Police Station and requested an investigation. When Mr. Xie Baosheng heard the news and rushed over, his beloved son had been kidnapped far away. It is said that Mr. Xie, although having a reputation, is outwardly strong but inwardly weak and has no savings. It is not known how this matter arose due to a misunderstanding. It is said that the kidnappers shouted for a ransom of 2,000 yuan when they left.

A Sad Outcome to a Westerner's Outing

▲ Car Plunges into River, Suffers Damage

▲ Soaked to the Bone, Luckily Uninjured

Yesterday afternoon around 3 o'clock, a Westerner, Mr. A, and his wife were driving their own car, license number 5129, to Wusong for sightseeing. They were enjoying themselves along the seaside, and around 6 o'clock, they started their return trip to Shanghai. When they reached the Zhanghuabang Station (at the bend of Jungong Road), due to excessive speed, the car flipped into the river. The car body was completely damaged, with the undercarriage facing up. Several telephone poles and trees, large and small, were hit and broken. Mr. A managed to climb out of the river, fortunately uninjured, but his clothing was soaked. He hired a car to return to Shanghai. The car in the river was placed under guard by two police officers dispatched by the local Public Security Bureau.

Bandit Wu Zunyi Sentenced to Five Years

The Jiangbei bandit Wu Zunyi, this spring, gathered a gang and armed with weapons, broke into Wanlong Sauce Garden at No. 632 Xujiahui Road in the French Concession and Maochangxiang Southern Goods Store at No. 142 Kangti Road, robbing them of silver dollars. They divided the loot and fled. Detectives and supervisors Jin Jiulin, Zheng Tanmu Li Yaolong, Bao Tan Zhou Buguang, Chen Jinshu, Xu Guilin, and others from the French Concession Police Station investigated, arrested Wu, and seized a pistol. They then arrested two suspects, Wang Axiao and Zheng Yuzhen, and brought them to the police station. Yesterday, they were taken to the French Court for trial. The plaintiffs, Wang Fuqing and Guo Yuanmao, testified about the circumstances of the robbery. When questioned, Wu Zunyi confessed to the robbery. Wang and Zheng testified that although they were acquainted with Wu Zunyi, they did not dare to commit robbery and requested a clear investigation. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Wu to five years in the Western prison, and upon completion, he would be permanently expelled from the concession. The seized pistol was confiscated. Wang and Zheng were found not guilty and released.

Yuanhe Pawnshop Fire Case Dismissed

The Yuanhe pawnshop opened by Yu Zhaosheng on Rue du Père Froc in the French Concession caught fire a few days ago. The Fire Brigade rushed to extinguish the fire. Afterwards, the police summoned Yu to the French Court for questioning. The court ordered an investigation into the cause of the fire before a decision could be made. Yesterday, Yu was summoned again. Mr. Bahe, the lawyer representing the defendant, Yu Zhaosheng, the owner of Yuanhe pawnshop, stated that the pawnshop had a very good business every year. Although it had fire insurance of 22,000 taels, the burnt goods were worth 60,000 to 70,000 gold yuan. The fire was caused by someone throwing a cigarette butt into the back window out of jealousy. He added that if evidence of this person is found in the future, they would be investigated and prosecuted. After deliberation, the Chinese and Western judges ruled that since it was confirmed that the fire was unintentional, the case would be dismissed.

Seamen's Union Relief for Refugees

▲ Seeking to Transport Them Back Home

▲ Over Ninety Men and Women

The Chinese Seamen's Industrial and General Union reported yesterday that the Guangdong branch had received a letter from the Guangzhou Municipal Social Bureau requesting assistance in transporting over ninety Shandong refugees, including Gao Gencao, back to their hometown. The union had contacted the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which arranged for the Guangda steamship to transport them to Shanghai. The original text of the letter is as follows: The Guangzhou Municipal Social Bureau stated, "According to Gao Gencao, a Shandong refugee, he and more than ninety others suffered from locust plagues and floods last year and drifted to this area. They are now camping in the open space in front of the Tianhou Temple in Caofang, Henan, and it is difficult to find food. As the spring farming season begins, they urgently want to return home to farm to avoid staying in a foreign land for a long time. However, they have no travel expenses and cannot return. They request assistance." After sending personnel to investigate, it was reported that there were a total of ninety male and female refugees, young and old. Some make and sell bamboo products or small toys to make a living, while others beg for a living. They are hungry and cold, and their situation is pitiful. When asked, all the refugees expressed their willingness to return to their hometown and should be helped. Therefore, this bureau is sending Li Yingjun and Mo Jing to your union to discuss the repatriation method. We hereby inform you and hope that you will contact us, discuss the matter properly, and respond accordingly. After approval, personnel were sent to the Guangdong branch of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which agreed to send the refugees to Shanghai on the Guangda steamship on the fifth of this month. The bureau was informed and ordered to handle the repatriation matters according to schedule and to inform the Shanghai Social Bureau to arrange for their transportation back to their hometown upon arrival. The handling of this case is hereby reported for your review."

Two Engineering Societies to Merge

Hu Shuhua, Xu Peihuang, Xue Cixin, members of the Chinese Institute of Engineers, and Hua Nangui, Xia Guangyu, Tang Zaixian, members of the Chinese Institute of Engineers, and Ling Hongzhu, Wei Yifu, Wang Shengshan, and other nine members of both societies, feel that it is necessary to unite the engineering academic organizations in our country, so they put forward a proposal for the merger and sent it to the members of both societies, hoping to resolve and realize it as soon as possible. After the merger, the total number of members of the two societies will be more than 5,000. The proposal is recorded below:

It is found that there are two domestic engineering academic organizations with a certain history and status. (1) The Chinese Institute of Engineers. (2) The Chinese Institute of Engineers. Their history and current status are approximately as follows: A. The Chinese Institute of Engineers was established in the early years of the Republic of China. The general headquarters are in Shanghai, and the branches are in Nanjing, Peiping, Tianjin, Qingdao, Hankou, Hangzhou, Jinan, Taiyuan, Suzhou, Fengtian, Wuzhou, and the United States. There are about 1,300 members, and some of them are self-employed industrialists and businessmen. The association publishes four issues of the association journal and one special issue of the association journal every month. There is a material testing laboratory in Shanghai, with a base and a fund of more than 20,000 yuan. B. The Chinese Institute of Engineers was initiated by Dr. Zhan Tianyou and others at the end of the Qing Dynasty. The general headquarters are in Peiping, and there are more than 400 members. Many of the seniors in the road industry are in it. It publishes one issue of the association bulletin every month. There is a general house in Peiping and some funds. In addition, the organization within the association, the qualifications of members, the collection of membership fees, and the progress of association affairs are similar, although the articles of association of the two associations are not exactly the same. The two associations have the same academic and professional standpoint, the same purpose, and a similar organization, and some of them are common members. However, because the organizations did not contact each other at the beginning, they went their separate ways. In the past, they were each in their infancy, and the two associations coexisted. In recent years, the construction industry has flourished, and the two associations have evolved for more than ten years and have a considerable position in the society. If they continue to have no contact with each other, it will have a major obstacle to the future of engineering academics, engineering careers, and engineering talents. The main points are as follows: (1) The organization is divided and cannot concentrate talents and careers to achieve the same goal. (2) There are members of the engineering community who are also members of the two associations, and it takes twice the effort to handle association affairs. (3) For suggestions and requests to the country or consultations belonging to the government and society, they cannot be expressed or dealt with as a whole. (4) For the liaison with domestic and international academic circles, there are two associations with the same nature, which are easy to confuse and cause estrangement. The proposers are members of the Jia association, members of the Yi association, or members of both associations. In order to concentrate the strength of the engineering community to seek the research progress of engineering academics and the observation and development of engineering careers, it is proposed to merge the Chinese Institute of Engineers and the Chinese Institute of Engineers into a national engineering institute, and request the immediate notification of all members by the two authorities to solicit their consent. At the same time, each association should organize a committee to study and proceed, and hold a joint congress of the two associations in the autumn of this year to resolve it in a suitable place. The main problems are as follows: 1. Name: Choose one of the original two names or set a new name outside the old name. 2. Location: Choose one of the two general headquarters as the location of the new general headquarters, and the others will be changed to new branch associations. 3. Membership qualifications: All members of the original two associations can be members of the new association. The membership qualifications will be re-established in the new chapter. 4. Articles of association: The committee will be dispatched by the two associations to study and draft the articles of association and submit them to the congress for approval. The proposers will send letters to the two associations requesting and informing all members of the two associations, and respectfully ask them to support with a far-sighted vision and a fair proposition. The proposers are Hu Shuhua, Xia Guangyu, Tang Zaixian, Hua Nangui, Xu Peihuang, Xue Cixin, Ling Hongxun, Wei Yiyu, and Wang Shengshan.

Municipal Government Publishes Summary of Municipal Administrative Statistics

The "Summary of Shanghai Special Municipal Administrative Statistics" published by the Municipal Government is the continuation of the Municipal Statistics Summary published in 1927. The data is derived from July 1, 1928, to June 30, 1929. The statistics contained in the book are limited to those related to the municipality. The editing style is divided into ten categories according to the nature of the affairs: (1) General Affairs, (2) Finance, (3) Land, (4) Society, (5) Public Works, (6) Public Security, (7) Health, (8) Education, (9) Port Affairs, (10) Public Utilities, with a total of approximately 300 charts and graphs, printed in color on Daolin paper with Western-style binding. The price is three silver dollars. The Commercial Press, Minzhi Bookstore, and the First Section of the Municipal Government all have copies for sale. There are also remaining copies of the 1927 Municipal Statistics Summary, priced at 2.40 silver dollars per copy.

Jisheng Association Relief Report on Yuhuan Spring Relief

The China Jisheng Association recently received a report from Yin Junshunzhang, a relief worker in Yuhuan, Zhejiang, stating that Yuhuan County, formerly under the jurisdiction of Wenzhou, is divided into three major districts: Jiangbei, Jiangnan, and Haishan. All are scattered islands, and transportation must be by帆船 or small wheel, and the mountains undulate, and the fall is scattered, and investigation is very difficult. The disaster situation is extremely serious, and the victims only rely on grass head and wheat tips to make soup to fill their hunger, and most of them are starving, without clothes or quilts, and they cannot cover their bodies with brown clothes and worn-out cotton wool. The life of the victims is not as good as that of cattle and horses. The county is isolated in the sea and has no production at all. Last winter, the sea was desolate, and the food relied on Leqing to help. Now Leqing cannot take care of itself, so yam chips can be bought for fourteen catties per 洋祖, and in the spring, 90 catties can be bought per 洋. The value has suddenly increased by more than 60%. The county has always been without wealthy households. Those with two or three hundred acres of land are the richest. The county's money and grain are only more than 10,000 yuan per year, and there is no political expense, schools are suspended, and more than 200 prisoners are short of food and cannot be maintained. The famine happens several times a day, bandits are everywhere, and the people's livelihood is worrying. The people are victims, the officials are victims, and there are about 30,000 households in the county. If strictly checked, 30% is calculated, and there are more than 12,000 households. This time, the amount of relief is only 30,000, and the average calculation is that each household will not receive more than 2 yuan. What is the point? The suffering is immense, and it is difficult to describe in writing. Can the amount of relief be appropriately increased to save the people from their suffering? We are very grateful. Recently, we received a telegram from Feng Ruoyangshan, the director of Zhejiang Relief Affairs, saying that the disaster in Yuhuan is terrible and requesting additional relief funds. The association is now raising funds to provide relief, but the disaster is widespread and the funds are insufficient, and we still need to appeal for help.

Kawasaki Company Adds Another New Ship

The Kawasaki Kisen Kaisha is taking advantage of the poor state of the Chinese shipping industry to expand its routes in an attempt to dominate coastal shipping rights. Last month, it added the Lukayama Maru, which runs between Shanghai, Wenzhou, and Fuzhou. Since its opening, business has been very prosperous. Recently, because most of the Chinese merchant ships on the North China route have been suspended, it intends to take this opportunity to develop North China shipping rights and decided to add a new ship, named the Kujirazaki Maru, with a deadweight of 2,350 tons. It sailed into Shanghai yesterday and is anchored in Pudong. It is scheduled to sail from Shanghai to Tianjin on the 27th of this month.

Municipal Finance Bureau Establishes Municipal Ship Tax Office

For the convenience of collecting ship taxes in the city, the Municipal Finance Bureau has specially established a Municipal Ship Tax Office to handle all ship tax matters in the city. The bureau has also drafted organizational rules and a budget for the expenses and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval. The rules are as follows: Article 1: The Shanghai Special Municipal Finance Bureau has established a Municipal Ship Tax Office in accordance with the provisions of Article 9 of the bureau's organizational rules for the purpose of collecting ship taxes in the city and handling all ship tax matters in the city. Article 2: The Ship Tax Office shall have the following staff: one director of section, several section members, several clerks, several accountants, several collectors, several inspectors, several ticket officers, and several secretaries. All the above staff, except for the director of section and the section members, who shall be appointed by the mayor upon the recommendation of the director of the bureau, the remaining staff shall be appointed or employed by the director of the bureau. Article 3: The director of section of the Ship Tax Office shall be subordinate to the Second Section of the bureau and shall manage all affairs within the office under the orders of the director of the bureau and the director of the supervising section. Each section member and clerk shall perform their respective duties and shall be subordinate to the directors of the supervising sections of the First, Second, Third, and Fourth Sections of the bureau and shall be stationed in the office to assist the director of section and manage all collection, audit, document, and general affairs within the office. Article 4: For the convenience of inspecting ships for tax evasion and collecting taxes, the Ship Tax Office shall, with the approval of the director of the bureau, establish branch offices at key overflow points of rivers and rivers, and shall酌設 staff to handle them according to the complexity of the affairs, and shall also establish inspections, send several inspectors, several boats, and several patrolmen to patrol regularly. Article 5: The tax collection time of the Ship Tax Office shall be in accordance with the regulations of the bureau's office hours. The office hours of the inspection shall be from dawn to dusk. At night, other boat patrolmen shall be assigned to shuttle and patrol. Article 6: The amount of tax collected by the Ship Tax Office every day shall be deposited into the bank or money shop designated by the bureau immediately after the collection is closed, and no later than 11:00 a.m. All receipts from the bank or money shop shall be sent to the bureau for review immediately. Article 7: The Ship Tax Office shall list the types and numbers of taxes collected every day and the number of tickets used separately and send them to the monthly report once for verification. The stored ticket stubs shall also be submitted to the bureau for verification at any time. Article 8: All tickets, receipts, and stamps used by the Ship Tax Office shall be printed and issued by the bureau. Article 9: The performance of the section members and clerks stationed in the Ship Tax Office by each section shall be evaluated by the directors of the supervising sections, and the director of section shall only be responsible for supervision and reporting. The performance of the remaining staff shall be evaluated by the director of section to clarify the limits of authority. Article 10: The diligence and laziness of the tax collectors of the Ship Tax Office shall be evaluated by the director of section once every month's end, and the advantages and disadvantages shall be listed and reported to the bureau for rewards and punishments. The rules for rewards and punishments shall be determined separately. Article 11: When shipowners resist taxation or other important matters occur in the Ship Tax Office, in addition to reporting to the bureau for verification, they may report to the nearby water and land police at any time and request assistance. Article 12: Each tax collector of the Ship Tax Office shall have a reliable business shop in this municipality to issue a reliable guarantee. In addition to the Ship Tax Office sending personnel to the First Section of the bureau for verification, they shall also be ordered to find another proper guarantee to guarantee everything in the event that the guaranteeing shop goes bankrupt or changes. Article 13: If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they may be submitted for revision at any time. Article 14: These rules shall be implemented from the date of submission to the Municipal Government

Approved.

Beixinjing Renamed Pusong Town

Since the establishment of the Municipal Government, the place names of the districts in this city have gradually become standardized. For example, Meijianong has been changed to Meilong, and Caohejing has been changed to Caojing, all taking the meaning to correspond to the district name and the town name. The Municipal Affairs Committee of Pusong District also submitted a request to change Beixinjing to Pusong Town the day before yesterday. The Municipal Government immediately ordered the Social Bureau to investigate and reply. Now, the Social Bureau has sent personnel to investigate and found that there is Wusong River in the north of the district and Puhuitang in the south. The name of the district is derived from this. The Municipal Affairs Office is located in Beixinjing Town, which is named after the Beixinjing Port, a tributary of the Wusong River. Now, it is proposed to change the town's name to Pusong Town. It is to seek consistency in the names of districts and towns. According to the general rule that place names are often named after a local mountain and river, the town should be named after Pusong rather than the name of a tributary of the Wusong River. It is extensive and appropriate, and it is also for the convenience of official document delivery and connection. It is not impossible to change Beixinjing to Pusong Town. It is heard that the Municipal Government has instructed to approve it.

Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation Solicits Zhejiang Disaster Relief Good Deeds Coupon Gifts

The Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation sent a letter to each factory the day before yesterday, which reads as follows: Dear Sir, We have recently received a letter from the Shanghai Special Municipal Commercial Reorganization Committee, which reads as follows: "The Zhejiang Relief Association in Shanghai stated that the disaster situation in Zhejiang Province this year is very serious. Our association plans to follow the example of raising funds for the Shandong disaster and issue good deeds coupons. We will first solicit items to be used as good deeds coupon gifts, and all the proceeds from the sale of the coupons will be used for relief. Since the beginning of the solicitation, charities at home and abroad have actively contributed, and many items have been solicited, but the amount is still far from the estimated amount. Although we have agreed with various national goods groups to organize temporary markets and sub-stations to solicit donations, the relief cause does not distinguish between nationalities. This city is a commercial port with Chinese and foreigners gathering, and all kinds of goods are abundant. Your association leads the commerce and is the general hub of Chinese and foreign countries. We hope that you will give priority to the Zhejiang disaster and give the utmost assistance to our association's solicitation of items. We urge all major stores and businesses to donate as many of the goods they sell or manufacture as possible, regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, and regardless of whether they are fine or crude. We hope that there will be as many as possible and that they will continue to come. We know that most of the merchants in Shanghai are deeply aware of the righteousness, and with your association's words, the effect will be as quick as a drum. The disaster victims in the two Zhejiangs will not be slightly benefited. Our association deeply cares about the disaster situation in our hometown, hears the cries of the victims, and is ashamed of not being able to do anything. We hope that you will listen to our request. We are grateful for your kindness." After the committee received the letter, it was decided at the 40th Standing Committee Meeting to ask each industry group to assist in the solicitation and to share the righteousness. We hereby inform you and ask you to pass it on to your members and solicit donations widely to contribute to the righteousness and benefit the victims. We hope that you will investigate.

Mrs. Tang Passed Away Yesterday Morning

The mother of Tang Shichang, a reporter for this newspaper, passed away due to phlegm and asthma at Maoshi yesterday morning. She was 62 years old. It is reported that the encoffining will be held at Weishi tomorrow (24th) at her residence at No. 489, Yonggui Lane,

Menara Road in this city. The funeral will be held at Weishi on the 25th. Mrs. Tang was diligent and thrifty in managing her household and was skilled in educating her children, and was consistently praised by relatives. Her sudden death has caused widespread mourning among those who knew her. Mr. Tang has a wide circle of friends, and it is expected that on the day of the funeral, simple carriages and white horses will be prepared with utmost honor.

Bandit Gao Zhengming Confesses to Robbery

Dong Mingde, a foreman of the first district of the South City, and detectives Yuan Haishan, Lü Anpu, and Cai Zhiqing, apprehended four bandits, including Wang A'er, on January 19th of this year. According to their confessions, Gao Zhengming and others were accomplices. The detectives have been investigating the case. Previously, they apprehended Gao near Xiaobeimen and brought him back to the district. The district chief Chen conducted a preliminary trial. According to Gao's confession, he is 22 years old, from Pudong, and currently resides at No. 19, Anren Lane, Kangti Road in the French Concession. He also confessed that Hu Boliang (also known as Rongyan), who is still at large, organized the gang to rob the Guo family at No. 4, Lane 79, Yaofang Lane, and that last winter, they robbed two households in Hengde Lane, Gaodun Road, and Yuyuli, Huacao Port. As the matter concerns robbery, he was ordered to prepare a document and submit it to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Shanghai Military Camp Robbery

The home of Yong native Wang Jiqiu, located at No. 23, Xinxian Lane, behind the former site of the Shanghai Military Camp in the South City, was robbed around 7 o'clock the night before last. Wang happened to be away. After dinner, Wang's father, Jianxiang, and Wang's wife were sitting in the living room. When the maid took a kettle and went out through the back door to fetch water, it is estimated that three bandits, two wearing Changqing-colored long robes and one wearing a blue robe, saw the back door ajar and seized the opportunity to enter. They stepped into the living room, and two bandits drew handguns, threatening them to remain silent. Two bandits guarded the front and back doors, while one bandit went upstairs, broke into the bedroom, rummaged through chests and drawers, and arbitrarily searched and robbed, taking 112 yuan in banknotes and foreign currency stored in the chests, as well as gold, silver, jewelry, and other ornaments, totaling over 400 yuan in value. The bandits then took the loot downstairs, gave a signal, and fled. Afterwards, Wang checked the exact amount of the losses and reported them to the first sub-station of the first district, requesting an investigation.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Hai Ke

▲Judge: I sentence you to three years in prison. Do you have anything to say?

Criminal: Please notify my wife that I won't be home for dinner tonight.

▲Husband: Will you listen to me? Let me explain.

Wife: I only need to listen to you in your dreams. Then I know everything.

▲Pickpocket A: Today I got a gold watch in the fog. It's worth a lot of money. What do you think?

Pickpocket B: Damn it, damn it. That's mine. What do you think of the diamond lapel pin I got?

Pickpocket A: Damn it, damn it. That's clearly mine.

▲Wife A: My husband has to go out every night. What do you think I should do?

Wife B: The only way is to go with him.

▲Girl A: My fiancé has been very cold to me lately. How should I punish him?

Girl B: Marry him quickly.

▲A: Why don't you live in your newly built house?

B: I can't afford to live there because the rent is too high.

Interesting Facts About Bicycles

— Meng Qi

The kind light of the goddess of spring has gradually shone upon people. In the fragrant breeze and warm sunshine, the most interesting outdoor sport is naturally cycling. Thinking about bicycles, I remember many interesting things.

In many places, the authorities do not allow women to ride bicycles. The reason is often that it is harmful to social morals. But when we think about it carefully, riding a bicycle is actually the most appropriate sport for women. However, abuses are naturally inevitable. For example, in the past, prostitutes in Hangzhou often rode bicycles to attract playboys. Therefore, the local authorities had to issue a ban.

A friend told me that a young man who was good at riding a bicycle met a girlfriend through racing. This girlfriend was also good at riding a bicycle. Later, because they shared the same interests, they got married. At the wedding, at the urging of the guests, the newlyweds were asked to compete in a bicycle race. The result was that the bride won. I think the groom must have conceded. Otherwise, this woman would have some real skills.

Generally, the most interesting time is when you first learn to ride a bicycle. For a few days before learning, you think about the bicycle almost day and night. Although you break your skin and bleed, you still can't give up. When you have practiced well, you feel that there is nothing interesting. Otherwise, those green-clad people who deliver red and green envelopes would be too happy. In fact, they are unspeakably miserable.

A small bicycle can have infinite changes. I used to visit the Hamerston Circus. The performing artist's bicycle was really magical. Sometimes he used his hands instead of his feet, sometimes he soared into the air, sometimes he went backwards, sometimes he stood up. The most interesting thing was that it was disassembled into two sections, leaving only one wheel. Yet the person could still move forward as usual. Isn't that strange?

I used to love riding a bicycle very much. Once, when I was riding back from my relatives' house, it was already dark. After riding for a while, because the road surface was uneven, I ran straight into the river. At that time, I thought I was doomed. But after I was submerged, I floated up again. I grabbed a handful of grass, trying to climb to the shore. Suddenly, it seemed like someone was pulling me from behind. I was really panicked. I wondered if there were really ghosts. Later, when I turned around and looked, I realized that my long gown was tied to the seat cushion. I couldn't help but laugh. Probably what the world calls ghosts and gods is nothing more than a psychological effect. In the end, my life was saved, but my long gown was torn. Since receiving this lesson, I have been afraid of bicycles whenever I see them. I no longer want to get close to them.

Hong Toutu and Shi Ziying jointly display the work of Yingbin publicizing the theme of Wanli Book.

Talking About Preparing for Air Defense

— Zhu Xing

China's unification has been achieved, and we must urgently prepare for security. Thinking back to the harm caused by airplanes dropping bombs on the border provinces, which extended for hundreds of miles, resulting in losses of millions, the border defense forces, although using machine guns, mortars, and anti-aircraft guns, etc., to attack fiercely, found it difficult to hit the targets. The reason is that the height and speed of the airplanes are beyond the reach of guns and cannons. Nowadays, various countries are expanding their air forces and producing sophisticated bombs, which will become the most powerful weapons in the world's future air wars. Therefore, Germany plans to build a large copper curtain, 300 yards high, divided into several layers, to place artificial smoke to obscure the sky, so that enemy aircraft will be at a loss. Mr. Jielie Pingsun proposed building cities underground to avoid the tragic end of being crushed to pieces. Various countries have made suggestions, and China, in light of the harm suffered by the border provinces, must also take immediate action. Therefore, it is proposed to create flying arrows, whose height and speed can surpass those of airplanes. When fired fiercely, aerial bullets and fire will erupt like a volcano. Even Germany's latest fighter aircraft will find it difficult to escape. If preparations for defense are not made in advance, the people filling the wilderness will have no survivors. The method of making the arrows will be explained separately. I hope our government will try to create these arrows as a plan to save the country and the people. In this way, the border can be consolidated, and the lives of the people can be secured. (Thanks for the contribution)

An Unconventional Photo Studio

— Xian

My old friend Shi Zishipan has set up a photo studio in Anlefang, at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Gordon Road. Although it is called a photo studio, it is actually a residence as well. I have heard of his name for a long time. A few days ago, I accompanied my old mother and brought my two children, Zheng and Ling, to visit him. I saw a small garden in front of the door, planted with several flowers. A young willow tree grew tall beyond the fence, its tender green branches bending as if to greet guests. The room was furnished with several tables and chairs, all in the latest modern style, simple and elegant. I heard that they were all designed by Mr. Jiang Xiaohu. The walls were decorated with various photos, mostly portraits, with the light being just right, unlike ordinary studios. These are all Shi Zizipan's masterpieces. Going upstairs, I saw the photo studio. The windows were covered with velvet curtains, and several lighting lamps were arranged around the room, all covered with white silk, providing clear but not dazzling light. The background was made of thick brown flannel, with hardly any creases. In the middle was a huge camera, with a German-made lens worth hundreds of gold, a rare item. Further in, a velvet curtain touched the ground, marking a makeup room. The dressing table was also new-style, exquisite and lovely, accompanied by gorgeous lamps and silk ornaments, as well as a nude beauty incense burner, all exquisitely beautiful, making people reluctant to leave. After touring around, Shi Zizipan took a photo of my old mother, then one of me and my two children, Zheng and Ling, guiding and directing the lighting meticulously. The next day, he showed me the film. The expressions were natural and lifelike. Shi Zizipan's artistic skill is evident. I admired it repeatedly and couldn't help but praise him.

Red Carpet

New Words on the Carpet

— Plum Blossom House Master

A month ago, various newspapers in this city widely reported that Cheng Yanqiu would withdraw from his singing and dancing career. The Jingang Pictorial even published a report that Yanqiu had already grown a beard. Recently, friends returning from the north mentioned that Yanqiu did indeed have a lukewarm attitude two or three months ago. However, after the persuasion of various bigwigs in the industry, he soon abandoned his preconceived notions and showed signs of taking the opportunity to form a troupe. Around that time, the Tianjin Xinxin Grand Theater sent someone to invite him. After repeated negotiations between the two parties, with the conditions not far apart, Yanqiu readily agreed. The rumors circulating for months that Yanqiu had stopped singing and changed careers were thus proven to be inaccurate. However, most of his original troupe members had already dispersed. People like Guan Dayuan, Hou Xirui, and Wang Youji had already joined other performers. It was impossible to gather them together for a while, so Yanqiu changed the roles of Guan and Wang, inviting Yan Jupeng and Jiang Miaoxiang to fill them, and also invited Hao Shouchun to help out temporarily to fill the gap left by Hou Xirui. The new troupe's cast is more complete than before. This time, Yanqiu led a large group of people to Tianjin to perform. It can be predicted that he will return with a good reputation.

Ms. Hua Huilin, famous in Shanghai, was taught her art by Little Zihe and Li Qinxian. Her style is proper and generous, combining the best of both. Last year, she went to Tianjin with her teacher to join a troupe. Her new voice was first tried, and she was praised throughout Tianjin. Newspapers and public opinion were particularly favorable. Now that the contract has expired, she returned to Shanghai by Shuntian wheel a few days ago. Teachers Feng and Li also returned to the south together.

Kun Ling Du Liyun's art has progressed rapidly since she worshiped Wang Yiyaoqing as her teacher, and her reputation has also been rising steadily. A month ago, she performed at the Huale Tea Garden in Xianyukou, and her beauty and reputation spread widely, rivaling Zhang Eyun and Jin Youqin. Starting this month, she will switch to performing at the Kaiming Cinema. Her future is bright and unlimited.

Hu Fangting, the manager of the Lida Stage in Hankou, came to Shanghai to invite Kun Ling Pan Xueyan, and the negotiations are about to be completed. At that time, rumors arose, and people were panicked. Xueyan was afraid that the situation in Hankou was unstable and that it would affect ticket sales. Therefore, she politely declined the trip to Hankou. It is rumored that Xueyan asked for too high a price and stopped the trip west, but this does not seem to be the real reason.

Xu Biyun, Gao Qingkui, and others will return north by boat soon.

Xun Huisheng, Guan Dayuan, and others will complete their term on the 24th and will not continue. They will return to Ping together at the end of the month.

Correspondence from European Travels (46)

— Liu Haisu

▲Andre Derain (2)

(Menglang's Work)

Now I want to talk about Derain. Derain's paintings have extraordinary authority and power in the modern European art world. In the Chinese art world, which is still too immature in its knowledge of new art, perhaps few people know this name.

During the heyday of Fauvism, Derain and Vaminck were called the two geniuses of the suburbs of Paris, probably by Maurice Denis. At that time, they both lived in Chatou. This seemed like an inseparable pair of lovebirds. Although youth combined the strong temperaments of the two, they had little in common spiritually. In fact, the distance between Derain and Vaminck is the distance between an artist with great ideals and an instinctive artisan of great talent. Moreover, when Denis spoke of Fauvism, he always listed the former as belonging to the famous [Geometric School], while he hardly mentioned the latter. Originally, the latter, like the former, came from art school. However, Derain had already demonstrated his profound cultivation on his first canvas. As for Vaminck's paintings, they were just the ordinary things seen by ordinary people. A kind of folk characteristic was very obvious. It has always been undeniable. Derain specialized in using the contrast of [surfaces] to make the picture appear subjective. In this respect alone, he stood parallel to Matisse. However, the great tradition of painting was closer to him than to the others. Derain's works, because of their various interests, contained many rare complexities. On the simple appearance, Derain was always an amazing writer.

If Matisse created a style of painting that was completed by a decorator, then Derain was the first person to be liberated from the entanglements of decoration. He skillfully expressed what he had practiced in Fauvism at that time, and sought out exposed tones. He once followed in the footsteps of Cezanne and discovered miracles that people had never noticed. He integrated all the techniques of this master of Aix, and then spied on the most mysterious places in art history. From then on, people constantly discussed his close relationship with the difficult reasoning and ancient meanings. Some said that it was a chaotic talent, wanting to melt the classical tradition and the primitive naivety into one furnace. It was a complex intellect, a kind of modulated intellectualism. He mixed the refined aesthetic concepts of the decadent artists of the late nineteenth century into the ancients' love of beauty. Primitive art sometimes used its symmetrical patterns to hypnotize him. He then gave it a certain charm. When he explored carefully, he gained a particularly humane way in the art of his peers. A method of communication that was clearer than a more foreign model. He was only influenced by the inherent decorative structure of some foreign models. He preferred to recreate the atmosphere of ancient sculptures and medieval gold-leaf paintings. Because he had a penchant for antiquity, he was fond of pure forms. For the spiritualistic art of the past, he was always fascinated. When he painted portraits, he brought a sweet harmony and a careful rhythm, sometimes with the smile of a primitive man. Like a bee, he sucked the flowers in the mysterious garden. Cimabue, Giotto, Fouguet, as well as the Mosaic writers and tapestry makers all gave this spiritual connoisseur pleasure. He retained in his heart a memorial of endless interest. It was not that the pictures created by his hands sometimes emitted a strange fragrance. It was that people understood the deep taste of modernism. In the deep harmony of his colors and the enthusiastic arrangement of his composition, he had foreseen the spirit of Gothic culture. The so-called Gothic style in his works was completed at the same time as the Great War. The spirit of primitivism on his canvases was also confirmed from then on.

American Cotton Short Sellers Heavily Covered Last Week

A telegram from New York dated the 21st reports on the cotton market during the week, stating that the situation in the Cotton Exchange last week was entirely short covering. The May price was particularly active at 1.04 yuan, until the May price reached 1.0564 yuan on Thursday. It is believed that this buying trend was driven by fellow traders covering, as well as short covering and position adjustments by traders both domestically and internationally, the amount of which was not small. Subsequently, the stagnation of transactions led to a slight reaction. Some short sellers were still strong in their attitude, but most had already covered. However, it seemed that the stagnation of transactions would depend on the development of the new cotton market or a good indication of the purpose of the May longs.

The telegram also reported that there was a risk of a short squeeze for the May and July contracts. The government seemed to be paying special attention to the cotton market. Butian retail sales were quiet, mostly due to the impact of high prices. Importers had no intention of buying smoothly. The arrival of Baiyuan goods was increasingly rare, and the buying interest was not as strong as the previous day. The market price was slightly firm.

▲ South Shanghai; Very few goods arrived downriver, totaling less than ten ships. Market sales were uneven. Prices of each group's machine-milled japonica rice were high, superior grades were stable, and particularly top-grade japonica rice was between 19.45 yuan. Foreign Rice Back in Circulation is Hoarding

Yesterday, the prices of foreign rice continued to rise. Because the foreign firms had no intention of selling, and there was even talk of settling a portion of the price, the market became even better, and goods back in circulation were hoarded. Prices of distant contracts rose by 3 to 4 fen each, and near-term contracts rose by 1 to 2 fen to nearly 1 jiao each. However, the street's sales were slightly weak after two new ships arrived with spot goods. Only customers from the interior and Wenzhou were still very active. As the street's appetite was dull, confidence returned to normal. A total of 1,000 bags of spot goods of Saigon number one sold for 15 yuan, 2,000 bags of small-grain rice sold for 14.5 yuan, and 3,000 bags of large-grain rice sold for 13.9 yuan. Secondary grades were priced lower. Futures rice included 1,000 tons of Saigon rice, 1,600 tons of small-grain rice, over 1,000 tons of large-grain rice, and 150 tons of Min Dang rice, all sold after being returned to circulation.

Optimistic Speculation Benefits the Flour Market

Yesterday, prices in the flour market were generally firm and rising. In March, April, and May, the market began to revert back to normal. Factory inventories were generally less than a month's worth, and prices were rising because, if the demand and sales of flour are relatively high during the shoulder months, there may be problems with supply and demand. Additionally, prices for key rice blends in both local and foreign ports are rising due to low inventories, and these conditions appear to be helping the flour market rise. Considering March and April contracts are no longer trading at a discount, the key to the future should be thought of in terms of actual conditions. New flour for distant months is trading at a higher premium because factories are not selling and customer sentiment is still good. As a result, the contract for this month and the April contract are trading one point higher than the previous day, the May contract is trading 1.25 points higher, the June contract is trading 2.5 points higher, the July contract is trading 5 points higher, and the August contract is trading 7.5 points higher.

Differing Prices of Wheat Futures

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw a mixed picture of rising and falling prices for various months. The current month started steady, but then bulls slightly reduced their positions. Shorts were preparing for physical delivery, causing the market sentiment to turn flat. For distant months, quotes for foreign wheat were up two to three cents for Chicago No. 2 and around seven cents for Canadian wheat, which greatly stabilized confidence. It's predicted that if shorts are indeed prepared for delivery this month, there shouldn't be any problems. As for new wheat futures, barring major weather events, the market value might have to be lowered a bit in the future. The result was a decrease of one cent for the current month compared to the previous day, an increase of one cent for April, one cent for June, no change for July, and one cent for August. The spot market was very quiet yesterday, as all high-quality goods were prepared for delivery. Lower-quality goods were not desired by factories. Only 400 bags of Nan Suizhou wheat were traded at 5 taels, 1 mace, and 2 fen.

Wenmingding, which had been firm for a long time, fell by 2.5 li, with Da Deli opening at 1 qian, 8 fen, and 2.5 li, and Meilanfang and Western Beauty both at 1 qian, 8 fen. The price of blue tiaoding remained level. Spot prices for fine bibby, Baoqiu assorted colors, and bald blue-gray fell again to 25 pieces, opening at 2 qian, 6 fen, and 2.5 li. White heavy French velvet has been in demand on this street recently, with Damo Lion selling for 2 qian, 3 fen and Fuhua for 2 qian, 2 fen and 5 li, mainly used for lining robes. Since the changing situation, Western goods sales in the north have been severely impacted. Those who intended to restock are now hesitant, especially for jacquard western yarn and tiaoziyusha. White chongtiao linen yarn has already fallen below 2 qian.

Social News

The Life of Native People in Southeast Asia - Jasmine

(3) Rules for Being a Husband

On the day of the wedding, the man must prepare another cow to show his goodwill. At the same time, this cow can be killed and used as a delicious feast for the guests. As a rule, before the wedding, the man has to go through a very long set of rituals. The native people especially consider the cow on the wedding day to be important. If he does not kill a cow to feed the guests on this day, no matter if he has had physical relations with this woman or has already raised children, others can still offer a higher price to buy his wife away. The Zulu people do not have a specific limit on the number of wives they can have. If he has cattle and can pay, he can marry as many as he likes. However, there is a rule for being a husband: he can marry many wives, but they must be treated equally. He is not allowed to love one and dislike another, and he must love them all fairly and universally, not love you more and love her less.

(4) Wives and Thatched Huts

When a man marries, he must live apart from his parents. However, the construction of a new house is still decided by his parents or elders. There are about three considerations regarding the location of the house: first, it cannot be too far from the hunting forest; second, there must be a clean piece of land near the new house where corn can be planted; and third, it must be within a few dozen steps of a pool where one can bathe forever. If such a location cannot be found, then a slightly worse location will do, as long as the raw materials for making native beer can be planted nearby. Their new house is really a thatched hut, with only a small door that lets in light. When entering the thatched hut, one must kneel and crawl in. Although this thatched hut is extremely simple, the mud floor inside is polished very clean.

Because a wife must have her own unique thatched hut, the more wives one marries, the more thatched huts there are. If their children grow up, their sleeping quarters must of course be separate. Therefore, prosperous native people have nearly twenty to forty thatched huts. We can also infer the number of wives a person has from the number of thatched huts. If he is a strong man, their thatched hut life is not lonely. He either goes hunting, sets traps to catch wild deer, digs rabbit holes, skins animals, or makes beer. Women, on the other hand, sometimes chop firewood, sometimes fetch water, sometimes cultivate the fields, and sometimes cook. The most regular task is to scrub the mud floor every fourteen days.

Children also have duties to fulfill in the family, which is to help their mothers chop firewood and fetch water. In addition, they go to the fields to watch out for monkeys and crows eating the food. When they grow up, their duties are the same as their father's. Girls, at the age of seven or eight, do household work. Boys at this age are responsible for herding cattle and sheep.

(5) A Wild Booze-Drinking Festival

Although the uncouth native people are now gradually assimilating with us, their ancient rituals are still prevalent. The most obvious is the booze-drinking of native beer. We have a servant named Nandi, who is also a native. He often goes to participate in this grand event in the evening. For those of us who do not know their lives, we often feel a strange interest in our hearts. We once asked him if we could participate and if we could photograph their wild revelry. They seemed to find our request interesting, so they readily agreed. We also promised to repay them with two wild animals. So the next day, we packed up our photography equipment and went together to the designated village. When we arrived, there was no sign of welcome at all. There wasn't even a dog in front of the door. We hesitated for a while, and suddenly felt panic in our hearts. What we feared was that the native people would object to our photography, so they had all avoided us before we arrived. After waiting for about half an hour, a beautifully dressed man came out of the haystack. He didn't seem to see us and walked straight into the thatched hut. We sat for a while and then secretly went to the front of the thatched hut to peek inside. We were startled to see a crowd of people packed inside, men, women, old, and young.

Their guests came in increasing numbers. Some of them recognized us and raised their hands to welcome us. By noon, they all came out of the thatched hut. At this time, a deer that we had brought was placed in front of them. None of them touched it until the second game arrived, and then they all skinned the animals together. They were very skilled at cooking. The water had already been fetched, and the firewood had been placed under the large iron pot. Inside the iron pot was twenty gallons of thick, milky white native beer. On top of the pot were dozens of bowls, each containing about a gallon of beer. When the game was almost cooked, everyone sat around the large pot. Several women took turns pouring the beer. They did not drink together by raising their glasses because there were too many people and not enough bowls to go around. Instead, one person would finish drinking and then hand the bowl to the person sitting next to them. The strangest thing was that they didn't say a word while drinking. Everyone was silent, especially at the beginning, and they observed solemn etiquette with each other. No one remained sober during this wild drinking. Once drunk, they had no restraints at all. Some laughed and joked, and some shouted, as if they had changed personalities. When we first saw their expressions, we didn't know what pleasure they had, but now we suddenly understood. After getting drunk, the circle they were sitting in also began to break. At this time, their women often stood up and danced. Her way of dancing was very different from ours in the West. When she was tired of dancing, another person would continue to dance. It is said that every woman has a different way of dancing, and each one is meant to express an emotion or an unrealized hope.

(6) The Dance of Gratitude

My wife and I sat on the side, watching their strange forms, and couldn't help but think of the terrible things that the preacher had told us when he returned from Africa. We were of different races and spoke different languages, so we could only sit and watch. When the women finished dancing, the men stood up again, preparing to dance the dance of gratitude together. They stood there, watching the oldest person dance first. The oldest person seemed to be the most respected person in their village. He danced to thank the sunlight for giving them light and warmth, and to thank the outsiders for participating in their festival with kindness. His dancing was not very long. After he finished dancing, he took the lead and guided everyone to sing together. At this time, the effects of the alcohol were very strong, and everyone sang and danced even more wildly because we were recording them. Unfortunately, it was getting dark and we couldn't take pictures. We left their dancing ground when the sun went down. My wife still laughs when she thinks about their wild revelry.

Dr. Japanese New Research on Having Boys and Girls

▲ Can the eternal mystery be further resolved?

The Japanese Medical Association will hold its eighth congress in Osaka in April. Professor Kawaka, a professor of obstetrics and gynecology, will explain the cause of the eternal mystery of having boys and girls. For two years, the professor used two to three thousand house mice to conduct detailed animal experiments based on the composition of food, drug injections, and other stimulating methods and conditions. Gradually, further solutions were obtained. It is said that [although hundreds of hypotheses have been proposed and thousands of experiments have been conducted to explain this eternal mystery, the iron gate is still not easy to open. The most powerful hypothesis, which is recognized by many people, is the explanation based on sex chromosomes, but it is difficult to explain all organisms with this]. Therefore, the professor put forward a unique hypothesis, saying that the conditions for sex determination are that the reproductive cells of both sexes generally have two groups that determine masculinity and femininity. The sex is also determined to be male or female depending on which side has more of the necessary elements. When the two groups for sex determination have equal strength, it will be determined by the influence of other third conditions. Based on this hypothesis, the experiments conducted by the professor can be divided into four types, such as giving food with various vitamins, a large amount of protein, and a large amount of salt, injecting secretions from endocrine glands, injecting Japanese food nerve poisons, and examining the effects of Reutgen rays. The test results are as follows:

(1) When females are given vitamin A and vitamin D and mated with ordinary males, they are more likely to produce male offspring.

(2) Giving females Clistanlin also results in more male offspring.

(3) When females are given ovarian secretions such as Ziskunengen and Aggeonengen, they are more likely to produce female offspring.

(4) When nerve poison is injected into both males and females, more male offspring are produced.

(5) When a white, toxic organic base is injected into a female, more female offspring are produced. When injected into a male, more male offspring are produced. When injected into both, the resulting offspring are half male and half female.

(6) When an organic base is given to a male and nerve poison is given to a female, more male offspring are produced.

(7) When nerve poison is given to a male and an organic base is given to a female, more female offspring are produced.

(8) When 4/9 of the male's skin has red spots, irradiation with Lian Gen rays shows a significantly higher chance of producing male offspring.

Regarding the above items, the professor said that the vitamin preparations and ovarian preparations are the two items that can be applied to people in this study. Other applications will be dangerous until future research is done.

Liang Quanwan on British Shipbuilding Industry

In recent years, the British shipbuilding industry has been struggling and striving desperately, just like other industries. The cruel and terrifying European War temporarily increased the demand for ships, but after the European War, this demand gradually decreased. Now, it is different again. In the past year or two, the British shipbuilding industry has made amazing progress, which is a remarkable achievement. In 1929, the total number of ships built in Britain reached 1,525,000 tons, an increase of 28,000 tons compared to the tonnage of ships built in 1928. To be honest, such a large tonnage is unprecedented in Britain. Last year, the total tonnage of ships built in Britain was 273,000 tons more than the total tonnage of ships built worldwide in 1929, which is a truly alarming amount.

Today, the demand for oil tankers is an undeniable fact, because they are easy to drive and the engine does not take up much space. There are currently 85 oil tankers being built worldwide, totaling 627,000 tons, 73 of which are powered by motor engines. However, Britain accounts for 54 of them, totaling 398,000 tons, which are currently under construction. Therefore, when calculated in detail, the total amount of oil tankers in Britain accounts for 63% of the world's oil tankers.
